<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Virgin Atlantic</h1>			<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
				<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>				<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p><b>Virgin Atlantic</b>, a <a href="/wiki/Trade_name" title="Trade name">trading name</a> of <b>Virgin Atlantic Airways Limited</b> and <b>Virgin Atlantic International Limited</b>, is a <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a> <a href="/wiki/Airline" title="Airline">airline</a> with its head office in <a href="/wiki/Crawley" title="Crawley">Crawley</a>, United Kingdom. The airline was established in 1984 as <i>British Atlantic Airways</i>, and was originally planned by its co-founders <a href="/wiki/Randolph_Fields" title="Randolph Fields">Randolph Fields</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alan_Hellary" title="Alan Hellary">Alan Hellary</a> to fly between <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a>. Soon after changing the name to Virgin Atlantic Airways, Fields sold his shares in the company after disagreements with <a href="/wiki/Sir_Richard_Branson" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Richard Branson">Sir Richard Branson</a> over the management of the company. The maiden flight from <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">Gatwick Airport</a> to <a href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_International_Airport" title="Newark Liberty International Airport">Newark Liberty International Airport</a> took place on 22 June 1984.
</p><p>The airline along with <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Holidays" title="Virgin Holidays">Virgin Holidays</a> is controlled by a holding company, Virgin Atlantic Limited, which is 51% owned by the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Group" title="Virgin Group">Virgin Group</a> and 49% by <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a>. It is administratively separate from other Virgin-branded airlines. Virgin Atlantic Airways Limited and Virgin Atlantic International Limited both hold <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Authority_(United_Kingdom)" title="Civil Aviation Authority (United Kingdom)">Civil Aviation Authority</a> (CAA) Type A Operating Licences (<a href="/wiki/Air_operator%27s_certificate" title="Air operator&#39;s certificate">AOC</a> numbers 534<sup id="cite_ref-AOC_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AOC-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and 2435 respectively),<sup id="cite_ref-AOC_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AOC-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> both of which permit these airlines, operating as Virgin Atlantic Airways, to carry passengers, cargo and mail on aircraft with 20 or more seats.<sup id="cite_ref-Licence_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Licence-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Virgin Atlantic uses a mixed fleet of <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Commercial_Airplanes" title="Boeing Commercial Airplanes">Boeing</a> <a href="/wiki/Wide-body_aircraft" title="Wide-body aircraft">wide-body aircraft</a> and operates to destinations in North America, the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, Africa, the Middle East and Asia from its main bases in London (<a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">Gatwick</a>), and its secondary base at <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester</a>. The airline also operates seasonal flights from <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Airport" title="Glasgow Airport">Glasgow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belfast_International_Airport" title="Belfast International Airport">Belfast</a>. Virgin Atlantic aircraft consist of three cabins: Economy, Premium (formerly <a href="/wiki/Premium_economy" title="Premium economy">Premium economy</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-:0_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and Upper Class (business).
</p><p>In 2012, Virgin Atlantic carried 5.4&#160;million passengers,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> making it the seventh-largest UK airline in terms of passenger volume. In the year to 31 December 2013, it reported a £51 million group pre-tax loss (approximately US$87 million),<sup id="cite_ref-Young2014_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Young2014-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> however, in the year to 31 December 2014 the airline reported a return to pre-tax profit of £14.4 million.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> In July 2017, Virgin Atlantic announced its intention to form a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Air_France-KLM" class="mw-redirect" title="Air France-KLM">Air France-KLM</a>. Under the agreement, Air France-KLM will acquire a 31 percent stake in Virgin Atlantic currently held by Virgin Group for £220 million.<sup id="cite_ref-partnership_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-partnership-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The deal is scheduled to be completed in early 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Atlantic_launch_press_conference.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Virgin_Atlantic_launch_press_conference.png/220px-Virgin_Atlantic_launch_press_conference.png" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Virgin_Atlantic_launch_press_conference.png/330px-Virgin_Atlantic_launch_press_conference.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/f/f3/Virgin_Atlantic_launch_press_conference.png 2x" data-file-width="388" data-file-height="257" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Atlantic_launch_press_conference.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Alan_Hellary" title="Alan Hellary">Alan Hellary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Branson" title="Richard Branson">Richard Branson</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Randolph_Fields" title="Randolph Fields">Randolph Fields</a> launch Virgin Atlantic at the 1984 press conference</div></div></div>
<p>Virgin Atlantic has its origins in a joint endeavour by <a href="/wiki/Randolph_Fields" title="Randolph Fields">Randolph Fields</a>, an American-born lawyer, and <a href="/wiki/Alan_Hellary" title="Alan Hellary">Alan Hellary</a>, a former chief pilot for British private airline <a href="/wiki/Laker_Airways" title="Laker Airways">Laker Airways</a>; following the collapse of Laker Airways in 1982, Field and Hellary decided to establish a new company, initially named <i>British Atlantic Airways</i>, as a successor.<sup id="cite_ref-Virgin_Birth_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Virgin_Birth-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Reportedly, Fields had formed a concept for an airline that would operate between London and the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a> during June 1982, when the <a href="/wiki/Falklands_War" title="Falklands War">Falklands War</a> had just finished.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Seeking out expertise in the field, Fields got in contact with Hellary, who had already been considering options for establishing a regular commercial service to the Falklands. In turn, Hellary was in contact with several out-of-work colleagues from the collapse of Laker Airways; as such, the pair decided to refine their ambitions.
</p><p>However, it was soon determined that the short runway at <a href="/wiki/Port_Stanley_Airport" title="Port Stanley Airport">Port Stanley Airport</a>, and the time it would take to improve it, would render a route to the Falklands commercially unviable, thus the idea of the such a service was dropped. In its place, Hellary and Fields commenced efforts to secure a licence to operate a route <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">Gatwick Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">John F. Kennedy International Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>. During May 1983, a three-day inquiry was conducted, which chose to reject the application following objections from <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Caledonian" title="British Caledonian">British Caledonian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport_Holdings" title="Heathrow Airport Holdings">BAA</a>.
</p><p>Hellary and Fields then applied for a licence between Gatwick and <a href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_International_Airport" title="Newark Liberty International Airport">Newark</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>, using a 380-seat <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_DC-10" title="McDonnell Douglas DC-10">McDonnell Douglas DC-10</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Virgin_Birth_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Virgin_Birth-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> However, faced with the prospect of direct competition from rival operator <a href="/wiki/People_Express_Airlines_(1980s)" title="People Express Airlines (1980s)">PEOPLExpress</a>, a post-<a href="/wiki/Deregulation" title="Deregulation">deregulation</a> "no frills" discount airline based at Newark, they decided to secure more funding before proceeding. Fields met with British entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Richard_Branson" title="Richard Branson">Richard Branson</a> at a party in London during which he proposed a business partnership. After protracted and testy negotiations, Fields agreed to a reduced stake of 25% in the airline (which was renamed <i>Virgin Atlantic</i>) and became its first chairman. Following disagreements over operations, Fields agreed to be bought out for an initial sum of £1&#160;million with further payment on Virgin's first dividend. As a result of a <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Justice" title="High Court of Justice">High Court</a> action, this additional payment was received shortly before Fields' death in 1997.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Formative_years">Formative years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Formative years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Atlantic_G-VIRG_by_Steve_Fitzgerald.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Virgin_Atlantic_G-VIRG_by_Steve_Fitzgerald.jpg/220px-Virgin_Atlantic_G-VIRG_by_Steve_Fitzgerald.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Virgin_Atlantic_G-VIRG_by_Steve_Fitzgerald.jpg/330px-Virgin_Atlantic_G-VIRG_by_Steve_Fitzgerald.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Virgin_Atlantic_G-VIRG_by_Steve_Fitzgerald.jpg/440px-Virgin_Atlantic_G-VIRG_by_Steve_Fitzgerald.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Atlantic_G-VIRG_by_Steve_Fitzgerald.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 747-200">Boeing 747-200</a> <i>Maiden Voyager</i> operated the first scheduled Virgin Atlantic service on 22 June 1984</div></div></div>
<p>On 22 June 1984, Virgin Atlantic operated its inaugural scheduled service, flown between Gatwick and Newark using a leased <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 747-200">Boeing 747-200</a> (registration <span class="nowrap">G-VIRG</span>), christened <i>Maiden Voyager</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Virgin_Birth_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Virgin_Birth-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> which had been formerly operated by <a href="/wiki/Aerol%C3%ADneas_Argentinas" title="Aerolíneas Argentinas">Aerolíneas Argentinas</a>. From the onset, its activities were augmented by leveraging existing <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Group" title="Virgin Group">Virgin Group</a> resources, such as tickets being sold at <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Megastores" title="Virgin Megastores">Virgin Megastores</a> outlets.<sup id="cite_ref-hilo_09_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hilo_09-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Part of Richard Branson's declared approach to business is to either succeed within the first year or exit the market; this ethos includes a one-year limit being expressed upon everything associated with starting up operations.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Virgin Atlantic became profitable within the first 12 months, aided by sister company <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Records" title="Virgin Records">Virgin Records</a>' ability to finance the <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_lease" title="Aircraft lease">lease</a> of a secondhand Boeing&#160;747. The firm had timed its operations to take advantage of a full summer, from June to September, which was typically the most profitable period of the year.
</p><p>In November 1984 the airline launched a service between Gatwick Airport and <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Aachen_Airport" title="Maastricht Aachen Airport">Maastricht Aachen Airport</a> in the Netherlands using a chartered <a href="/wiki/BAC_One-Eleven" title="BAC One-Eleven">BAC One-Eleven</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1986 the airline added another Boeing&#160;747 to its fleet and started a scheduled route from Gatwick to <a href="/wiki/Miami_International_Airport" title="Miami International Airport">Miami</a>. Additional aircraft were quickly acquired and new routes launched from Gatwick, such as to <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">New York JFK</a> in 1988, <a href="/wiki/Narita_International_Airport" title="Narita International Airport">Tokyo</a> in 1989, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport" title="Los Angeles International Airport">Los Angeles</a> in 1990, <a href="/wiki/Logan_International_Airport" title="Logan International Airport">Boston</a> in 1991, and <a href="/wiki/Orlando_International_Airport" title="Orlando International Airport">Orlando</a> in 1992. During 1987, Virgin Atlantic launched a service between <a href="/wiki/London_Luton_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Luton Airport">Luton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Airport" title="Dublin Airport">Dublin</a> using secondhand <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount" title="Vickers Viscount">Viscount</a> <a href="/wiki/Turboprop" title="Turboprop">turboprop</a> aircraft, but this route was withdrawn around 1990. During 1988, <a href="/wiki/Club_Air" title="Club Air">Club Air</a> operated two <a href="/wiki/Boeing_727" title="Boeing 727">Boeing&#160;727</a> <a href="/wiki/Jet_aircraft" title="Jet aircraft">jet aircraft</a> on behalf of Virgin; these served the Luton to Dublin route until about 1990.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Competition">Competition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Competition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg" class="image"><img alt="Text document with red question mark.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/40px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/60px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/80px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>possibly contains inappropriate or misinterpreted <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:CITE" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:CITE">citations</a> that do not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:V" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:V">verify</a> the text</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by checking for citation inaccuracies.</span>  <small><i>(September 2015)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A340-311,_Virgin_Atlantic_Airways_AN0062857.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Airbus_A340-311%2C_Virgin_Atlantic_Airways_AN0062857.jpg/220px-Airbus_A340-311%2C_Virgin_Atlantic_Airways_AN0062857.jpg" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Airbus_A340-311%2C_Virgin_Atlantic_Airways_AN0062857.jpg/330px-Airbus_A340-311%2C_Virgin_Atlantic_Airways_AN0062857.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Airbus_A340-311%2C_Virgin_Atlantic_Airways_AN0062857.jpg/440px-Airbus_A340-311%2C_Virgin_Atlantic_Airways_AN0062857.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="476" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A340-311,_Virgin_Atlantic_Airways_AN0062857.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Airbus_A340#A340-300" title="Airbus A340">Airbus A340-300</a> landing at <a href="/wiki/Kai_Tak_Airport" title="Kai Tak Airport">Kai Tak Airport</a>, displaying the "No Way BA/AA" sticker</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Atlantic_A340-300_G-VHOL_LHR_2003-6-12.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Virgin_Atlantic_A340-300_G-VHOL_LHR_2003-6-12.png/220px-Virgin_Atlantic_A340-300_G-VHOL_LHR_2003-6-12.png" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Virgin_Atlantic_A340-300_G-VHOL_LHR_2003-6-12.png/330px-Virgin_Atlantic_A340-300_G-VHOL_LHR_2003-6-12.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Virgin_Atlantic_A340-300_G-VHOL_LHR_2003-6-12.png/440px-Virgin_Atlantic_A340-300_G-VHOL_LHR_2003-6-12.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="790" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Atlantic_A340-300_G-VHOL_LHR_2003-6-12.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Airbus_A340#A340-300" title="Airbus A340">Airbus A340-300</a> at <a href="/wiki/London_Heathrow_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Heathrow Airport">London Heathrow Airport</a> in 2003, displaying "4 Engines 4 Longhaul" slogan</div></div></div>
<p>Before its inception, British Airways had been the only airline from the United Kingdom serving long-haul routes to destinations in North America, the Caribbean and the Far East since the <a href="/wiki/British_Caledonian_in_the_1980s#British_Airways_wins_the_day" title="British Caledonian in the 1980s">BA-BCal merger</a> in the late 1980s. In 1991, Virgin was given permission to operate from Heathrow following the abolition of the London Air Traffic Distribution Rules (TDRs) which had governed the distribution of traffic between Heathrow and Gatwick airports since 1978, primarily to bolster the profitability of Gatwick. Airlines without an international scheduled service from Heathrow prior to 1 April 1977 were obliged to operate from Gatwick. However, airlines that did not already operate at Heathrow were still able to begin domestic scheduled services there provided BAA, which ran both Heathrow and Gatwick on behalf of the UK Government, and the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Transport" title="Secretary of State for Transport">Secretary of State for Transport</a> granted permission.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Authority_(United_Kingdom)" title="Civil Aviation Authority (United Kingdom)">Civil Aviation Authority</a> also transferred two pairs of unused <a href="/wiki/Landing_slot" title="Landing slot">landing slots</a> that British Airways held at Tokyo's <a href="/wiki/Narita_International_Airport" title="Narita International Airport">Narita Airport</a> to Virgin to let it increase its frequency between Heathrow and Tokyo from four to six weekly round trips, making it easier for Virgin to compete against British Airways. The then-Chairman of BA <a href="/wiki/John_King,_Baron_King_of_Wartnaby" title="John King, Baron King of Wartnaby">Lord King</a> called the CAA's decision, which the Government had endorsed, "a confiscation of his company's property".<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the year to October 1993, Virgin Atlantic declared a loss of £9.3m. The decision to abolish the London TDRs and to let Virgin Atlantic operate at Heathrow in competition with British Airways became the trigger for BA's so-called "dirty tricks" campaign against Virgin. During 1993, BA's <a href="/wiki/Public_relations" title="Public relations">public relations</a> director, <a href="/wiki/David_Burnside" title="David Burnside">David Burnside</a>, published an article in <i>BA News</i>, British Airways' internal magazine, which argued that Branson's protests against British Airways were a publicity stunt. Branson sued British Airways for libel, using the services of <a href="/wiki/George_Carman" title="George Carman">George Carman</a> <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Counsel" title="Queen&#39;s Counsel">QC</a>. BA settled out of court when its lawyers discovered the lengths to which the company had gone in trying to kill off Virgin. British Airways had to pay a legal bill of up to £3&#160;million, damages to Branson of £500,000 and a further £110,000 to his airline. Branson reportedly donated the proceeds from the case to Virgin Atlantic staff.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the 1990s, Virgin Atlantic jets were painted with "No Way BA/AA" as a declaration of its opposition to the attempted merger between British Airways and <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> In 1997, following British Airways' announcement that it was to remove the <a href="/wiki/Union_Flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Union Flag">Union Flag</a> from its tailfins in favour of <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_ethnic_liveries" title="British Airways ethnic liveries">world images</a>, Virgin introduced a Union Flag design on the <a href="/wiki/Wingtip_device#Winglet" title="Wingtip device">winglets</a> of its aircraft and changed the red dress on the <i>Scarlet Lady</i> on the nose of aircraft to the union flag with the tag line "Britain's <a href="/wiki/Flag_Carrier" class="mw-redirect" title="Flag Carrier">Flag Carrier</a>". This was a tongue-in-cheek challenge to BA's traditional role as the UK's flag carrier.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2006, US and UK competition authorities investigated alleged <a href="/wiki/Price_fixing" title="Price fixing">price fixing</a> between Virgin Atlantic and British Airways over passenger fuel surcharges.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In August 2007, BA was fined £271&#160;million by the UK <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Fair_Trading" title="Office of Fair Trading">Office of Fair Trading</a> (OFT) and the US&#160;<a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">Department of Justice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> However, the Chief Executive of Virgin Atlantic, Steve Ridgway, was forced to admit that the company had been a party to the agreement, had been aware of the price fixing and had taken no steps whatsoever to stop the price fixing.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The company escaped a similar fine to that levied on British Airways only by virtue of the immunity it had earlier negotiated with the regulators.
</p><p>In April 2010, a tip-off from <a href="/wiki/Cathay_Pacific" title="Cathay Pacific">Cathay Pacific</a> led to the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Fair_Trading" title="Office of Fair Trading">Office of Fair Trading</a> (OFT) investigating alleged price fixing between Virgin Atlantic and <a href="/wiki/Cathay_Pacific" title="Cathay Pacific">Cathay Pacific</a> on flights to Hong Kong between 2002 and 2006. Cathay Pacific received immunity from prosecution for reporting the alleged offence. A maximum fine, if found guilty, was 10% of turnover which based on the £2.5&#160;billion in sales for the year to February 2009 would have been £250&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> At the time, the OFT stressed that it should not be assumed that the parties involved had broken the law.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The OFT cleared both airlines in December 2012, concluding there were "no grounds for action".<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_years">Recent years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Recent years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In May 2014 Virgin Atlantic ended flights to Sydney. In September 2014 Virgin Atlantic announced plans to scrap flights to Tokyo, Mumbai, Vancouver and Cape Town, and to <a href="/wiki/Codesharing" class="mw-redirect" title="Codesharing">codeshare</a> transatlantic flights with <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a>; the company was also reported to be considering axing its new 'Little Red' domestic airline after suffering heavy losses.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_little_red_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph_little_red-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> On 6 October 2014, Virgin Atlantic confirmed that Little Red services between London and Manchester would end in March 2015, and that the Scottish routes would be terminated in September 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Passengers used the routes from point to point as opposed to using it as a connection for longer haul Virgin Atlantic flights. The former BMI routes will continue with rival airline British Airways.
</p><p>In June 2015, Richard Branson admitted that Virgin Atlantic would be in "real trouble" without strategic support from <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a>. With cumulative losses between 2010 and 2013 amounting to £233 million, the future of the 30-year-old airline was in doubt.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In the same month, the airline announced it would cut 500 jobs to establish a more efficient management structure.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2017, Virgin Atlantic announced its intention to form a joint venture with Air France-KLM. Under the agreement, Air France-KLM will acquire a 31 percent stake in Virgin Atlantic currently held by Virgin Group for £220 million subject to execution of definitive agreements and receipt of final shareholder, board, and regulatory approvals. Virgin Atlantic would retain its independence as a UK airline with a UK operating certificate, and will continue to fly under the Virgin brand.<sup id="cite_ref-partnership_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-partnership-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2018, Virgin Atlantic announced they will end flights to Dubai in March 2019, citing the economic climate and low demand.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Offices">Offices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Offices">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Atlantic_HQ,_Manor_Royal,_Crawley.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Virgin_Atlantic_HQ%2C_Manor_Royal%2C_Crawley.JPG/220px-Virgin_Atlantic_HQ%2C_Manor_Royal%2C_Crawley.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Virgin_Atlantic_HQ%2C_Manor_Royal%2C_Crawley.JPG/330px-Virgin_Atlantic_HQ%2C_Manor_Royal%2C_Crawley.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Virgin_Atlantic_HQ%2C_Manor_Royal%2C_Crawley.JPG/440px-Virgin_Atlantic_HQ%2C_Manor_Royal%2C_Crawley.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Atlantic_HQ,_Manor_Royal,_Crawley.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The former head office building <i>The Office</i> in <a href="/wiki/Crawley" title="Crawley">Crawley</a></div></div></div>
<p>Virgin Atlantic's head office, known as <i>The Base</i>, is located on a business park in <a href="/wiki/Crawley" title="Crawley">Crawley</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">Gatwick Airport</a><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> and also houses the corporate offices of <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Holidays" title="Virgin Holidays">Virgin Holidays</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The company operates several offices and call centres around the United Kingdom, including a large office in <a href="/wiki/Swansea" title="Swansea">Swansea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>, which is a base for reservations and sales, baggage claims and tracing, 'live chat' web support and a customer relations department.
</p><p>International offices are located at <a href="/wiki/Norwalk,_Connecticut" title="Norwalk, Connecticut">Norwalk</a>, Johannesburg, Barbados, Shanghai, Hong Kong, Greater Delhi, Lagos and Dubai.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ownership">Ownership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Ownership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Virgin Group sold a 49% stake in the airline to <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a> in 1999 for £600&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> On 14 May 2008, Singapore Airlines formally announced an invitation for offers for its Virgin Atlantic stake, and publicly acknowledged that its stake in the airline had "underperformed".<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2010 it was reported that Virgin Atlantic had appointed <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank" title="Deutsche Bank">Deutsche Bank</a> to begin a strategic review of options for the airline following the tie-up between British Airways and American Airlines.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> By February 2011 it was confirmed that <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a> members <a href="/wiki/Air_France-KLM" class="mw-redirect" title="Air France-KLM">Air France-KLM</a> and Delta Air Lines had appointed <a href="/wiki/Goldman_Sachs" title="Goldman Sachs">Goldman Sachs</a> to advise them on a joint potential approach for Virgin Atlantic. <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways</a> was also reported to be considering a deal,<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Willie_Walsh_(Irish_businessman)" class="mw-redirect" title="Willie Walsh (Irish businessman)">Willie Walsh</a>, chief executive of <a href="/wiki/International_Airlines_Group" title="International Airlines Group">International Airlines Group</a>, stated that they would be interested in the airline, but only for the lucrative take-off and landing slots it holds at Heathrow Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 11 December 2012, Delta Air Lines confirmed the purchase of Singapore Airlines' 49% stake in Virgin Atlantic for £224 million, with plans to develop a transatlantic joint venture. Regulatory approval from the United States and European Union was granted on 20 June 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> and the purchase was completed on 24 June.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> In December 2012, <a href="/wiki/International_Airlines_Group" title="International Airlines Group">International Airlines Group</a> CEO, Willie Walsh, suggested that the loss-making company would be history within five years. "I can't see Delta wanting to operate the Virgin brand because if they do what does that say about the Delta brand? I just don't see that the guy [Branson] has anything that stands out in terms of what he has achieved in the industry."<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2017, Virgin Group agreed to sell a 31% stake in the airline to Air France-KLM for £220 million, leaving it with a 20% holding.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The deal is scheduled to be completed in early 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_trends">Business trends</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Business trends">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Service_concept">Service concept</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Service concept">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_lounge,_Heathrow.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Virgin_lounge%2C_Heathrow.jpg/220px-Virgin_lounge%2C_Heathrow.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Virgin_lounge%2C_Heathrow.jpg/330px-Virgin_lounge%2C_Heathrow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Virgin_lounge%2C_Heathrow.jpg/440px-Virgin_lounge%2C_Heathrow.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_lounge,_Heathrow.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Clubhouse</i> lounge at <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow Airport</a></div></div></div>
<p>Virgin Atlantic aircraft operate with a three-class cabin configuration: <a href="/wiki/Economy_Class" class="mw-redirect" title="Economy Class">Economy</a>, Premium (formerly <a href="/wiki/Premium_Economy" class="mw-redirect" title="Premium Economy">Premium economy</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-:0_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and Upper Class - the <a href="/wiki/Business_class" title="Business class">business class</a> product. Premium Economy has a separate check-in area, priority boarding and a wider seat with more legroom. Upper Class features a seat that converts into a fully flat bed and access to chauffeur drive.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Virgin Atlantic was the first airline to offer personal entertainment for all passengers in all classes.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The airline's <a href="/wiki/Frequent-flyer_program" title="Frequent-flyer program">frequent-flyer program</a> is styled 'the Flying Club'.
</p><p>Virgin Atlantic operates ten <a href="/wiki/Airport_lounge" title="Airport lounge">lounges</a> worldwide. It has nine 'Clubhouse' locations - London (Heathrow and Gatwick), New York-JFK, Newark, Boston, Washington D. C., San Francisco, Los Angeles and Johannesburg.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> It also maintains a 'Revivals' arrival lounge in London Heathrow. They are accessible for passengers travelling in Upper Class and Flying Club Gold tier members.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Little_Red">Little Red</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Little Red">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic_Little_Red" title="Virgin Atlantic Little Red">Virgin Atlantic Little Red</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Atlantic_Airbus_A320-214;_EI-EZW@LHR;13.05.2013_708fk_(8738115862).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Virgin_Atlantic_Airbus_A320-214%3B_EI-EZW%40LHR%3B13.05.2013_708fk_%288738115862%29.jpg/220px-Virgin_Atlantic_Airbus_A320-214%3B_EI-EZW%40LHR%3B13.05.2013_708fk_%288738115862%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Virgin_Atlantic_Airbus_A320-214%3B_EI-EZW%40LHR%3B13.05.2013_708fk_%288738115862%29.jpg/330px-Virgin_Atlantic_Airbus_A320-214%3B_EI-EZW%40LHR%3B13.05.2013_708fk_%288738115862%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Virgin_Atlantic_Airbus_A320-214%3B_EI-EZW%40LHR%3B13.05.2013_708fk_%288738115862%29.jpg/440px-Virgin_Atlantic_Airbus_A320-214%3B_EI-EZW%40LHR%3B13.05.2013_708fk_%288738115862%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3363" data-file-height="2234" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Atlantic_Airbus_A320-214;_EI-EZW@LHR;13.05.2013_708fk_(8738115862).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Virgin Atlantic <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A320-200">Airbus A320-200</a> <i>Little Red</i> operated by Aer Lingus</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/British_Midland_International" title="British Midland International">British Midland International</a> provided domestic and European feeder traffic into Heathrow Airport in partnership with Virgin<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> until it was purchased by British Airways' parent company <a href="/wiki/International_Airlines_Group" title="International Airlines Group">International Airlines Group</a> in 2011. The <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a>-owned airline had faced heavy annual losses of more than £100 million. Under the terms of the takeover, IAG had to relinquish some former BMI domestic slots at Heathrow. Virgin Atlantic purchased enough slots in 2012 to enable it to launch a domestic service on 31 March 2013, under the "Little Red" brand, operating a total of 12 daily services from London to <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen_Airport" title="Aberdeen Airport">Aberdeen</a> (3), <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Airport" title="Edinburgh Airport">Edinburgh</a> (6), and Manchester (3).<sup id="cite_ref-Domestic_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Domestic-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The airline <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_lease" title="Aircraft lease">wet-leased</a> four Airbus <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A320-200">Airbus A320-200s</a> from <a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus" title="Aer Lingus">Aer Lingus</a>, operating with Virgin Atlantic livery, under a three-year contract.<sup id="cite_ref-Lingus_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lingus-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2014, it was reported that Virgin was considering closing its domestic brand after suffering heavy losses,<sup id="cite_ref-Little_Red_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Little_Red-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Authority_(United_Kingdom)" title="Civil Aviation Authority (United Kingdom)">Civil Aviation Authority</a> figures confirming an average seat occupancy level of just 37.6% in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_little_red_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph_little_red-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The 12 daily pairs of take-off and landing slots at Heathrow cannot be sold to be used for long-haul routes.<sup id="cite_ref-BMIslots_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BMIslots-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 6 October 2014, Virgin confirmed that the Little Red service would cease; flights to Manchester ended on 28 March 2015 and flights to Edinburgh and Aberdeen ended on 26 September 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Virgin_Atlantic_International_Limited">Virgin Atlantic International Limited</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Virgin Atlantic International Limited">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 13 April 2015, Virgin Atlantic incorporated a new subsidiary - Virgin Atlantic International Limited (VAIL).<sup id="cite_ref-VAIcompany_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VAIcompany-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> In November 2015, VAIL obtained its own <a href="/wiki/Air_operator%27s_certificate" title="Air operator&#39;s certificate">Air Operators Certificate</a> and Operating Licence, and commenced operations with two former Virgin Atlantic Airways Limited operated <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330-300" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A330-300">Airbus A330-300</a> aircraft taking over routes previously operated by Virgin Atlantic Limited between London Gatwick and Barbados, St Lucia, Antigua, Grenada and Tobago.<sup id="cite_ref-VAIL_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VAIL-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> These flights are operated on behalf of Virgin Atlantic.<sup id="cite_ref-VAIL2_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VAIL2-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Upon incorporation as an AOC holder, the majority of Virgin Atlantic's landing slots at London Heathrow Airport were transferred to VAIL, allowing Virgin to access the value of the carriers slots by '<a href="/wiki/Mortgage_loan" title="Mortgage loan">mortgaging</a>' them through open investment from capital markets, the first time in Europe a company has used airport take-off and landing slots to generate money in this way.<sup id="cite_ref-Slots_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Slots-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Slots2_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Slots2-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fleet">Fleet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Fleet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:G-VINE_A330_Virgin_Atlantic_by_Mark_Harkin.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" 787-9</a>, on approach to <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">London Heathrow Airport</a></div></div></div></div>
<p>Virgin Atlantic uses a mixed fleet of <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Commercial_Airplanes" title="Boeing Commercial Airplanes">Boeing</a> aircraft. All the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">Boeing 747-400s</a> are based at Gatwick and Manchester and operate routes to Orlando, Las Vegas and the Caribbean (Gatwick only); <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330" title="Airbus A330">Airbus A330</a>-300s are also used on selected routes from Gatwick to the Caribbean. The Airbus A330-300s also operate from <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester</a> to New York-JFK, Boston, Atlanta and San Francisco. <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Airport" title="Glasgow Airport">Glasgow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belfast_International" class="mw-redirect" title="Belfast International">Belfast International Airport</a> offer a seasonal route to Orlando using Boeing 747s. Airbus A330s, Airbus A340s and Boeing 787s are used interchangeably on routes from London Heathrow Airport. In August 2002, Virgin became the first airline to operate the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A340-600" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A340-600">Airbus A340-600</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 27 September 2006, Branson announced plans to reduce <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> emissions by cutting aircraft weight and fuel consumption. There was also an experiment in 2007 in partnership with Boeing to have aircraft towed to the runway to save fuel, as a potential change to future operational procedures.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Virgin also volunteered a Boeing 747 for a test of <a href="/wiki/Biofuels" class="mw-redirect" title="Biofuels">biofuels</a> in February 2008. The aircraft flew without passengers from Heathrow to <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol" title="Amsterdam Airport Schiphol">Amsterdam Airport Schiphol</a>, with 20% of the power for one engine provided by plant-based biofuel. Virgin said that it expected to use <a href="/wiki/Algae" title="Algae">algae</a>-based biofuels in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Virgin Atlantic took delivery of its first <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787-9" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 787-9">Boeing 787-9</a> in October 2014, becoming the first European airline to fly the variant.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Virgin's order was first announced on 24 April 2007, and is for a total of 17 aircraft, with <a href="/wiki/Option_(aircraft_purchasing)" title="Option (aircraft purchasing)">options</a> on five more. The exercised options will replace the Heathrow-based 747 fleet during 2015 and 2016. Virgin Atlantic had also ordered 6 of the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380-800" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A380-800">Airbus A380-800</a> aircraft, with options on a further six, delivery initially due in 2006. This order was officially cancelled in March 2018, with deposits transferred to A330 and A350 aircraft orders.
</p><p>The older Airbus A340-300 aircraft were withdrawn from service in April 2015, as rising costs had made it less economical to run the type. Virgin had begun to replace the A340-300 on routes with the two-engine A330-300 and 787-9. The final Virgin Atlantic A340-300 flight was made on 9 April, landing at Heathrow early on 10 April.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Eight A340-600s remain in service.
</p><p>The airline's A330s, in three-class layout, have been stationed at Heathrow Airport since April 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sir Richard Branson announced in March 2016 that <a href="/wiki/The_Spaceship_Company" title="The Spaceship Company">The Spaceship Company</a> would partner with <a href="/wiki/Boom_Technology" title="Boom Technology">Boom Technology</a> to develop supersonic jets capable of travelling between London and New York in three and a half hours. He confirmed that Virgin Atlantic had options on ten of the aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2016, Virgin Atlantic announced an order for 12 <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350_XWB" title="Airbus A350 XWB">Airbus A350-1000</a> aircraft, to eventually replace the ageing 4-engined <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">Boeing 747-400</a> and <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A340" title="Airbus A340">Airbus A340-600</a> fleets. The order consists of 8 aircraft which will be purchased directly from <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a>, with a further 4 acquired through leasing companies. It is expected that the 12 A350-1000s on order will be split into 2 separate configurations, a business-oriented, premium heavy configuration, and leisure-oriented, economy heavy configuration for select routes to the Caribbean, Las Vegas, and Orlando, Florida. The first aircraft is scheduled to be delivered in 2019, with the Rolls-Royce XWB engine selected (the only available option for the Airbus A350 line-up). This order will leave Virgin with a streamlined fleet of Airbus A330s, A350s and Boeing 787 aircraft, leaving just 2 pilot pools and increasing cost efficiencies.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Due to engine fan-blade corrosion issues with Virgin's fleet of <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">Boeing 787</a> aircraft, Virgin Atlantic has chosen to move some of its <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester</a>-based Boeing 747 and Airbus A330 aircraft to cover routes out of London Heathrow. In 2016, A spokesman for Rolls Royce which manufacturers the Trent 1000s said the company "would start producing new corrosion-resistant fan blades by the start of 2017". Virgin Atlantic has had to temporarily park some of its 787s while they wait for attention. In place of these aircraft Virgin Atlantic has chosen to lease 4 former <a href="/wiki/Air_Berlin" title="Air Berlin">Air Berlin</a> A330-200 aircraft, which will be based out of Manchester. The A330-200 aircraft will arrive from 2018, with full Virgin Atlantic liveries, but with former Air Berlin cabin products, with Virgin Atlantic’s Premium Economy to be retrofitted at a later date. Virgin Atlantic said it would add "resilience" to its fleet after the engine issues with its 787s. It is thought these aircraft will be on initial 12 month leases, to allow Virgin to assess their viability in the fleet, with the possibility of extending the leases further.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The airline has also chosen to reinstate a former A340-600 aircraft "G-VNAP" into the fleet from storage, after purchase from its lessor, to cover for one A340 aircraft leaving the fleet, for which the lease was unable to be extended.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2018, <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a> announced the cancellation of Virgin Atlantic's order for six <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380-800" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A380-800">Airbus A380-800s</a> which it had placed back in 2001 and deferred several times since.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On May 4, 2018 'The VS Source' reported the return of a further A340-600, "G-VWIN" aircraft to the fleet, following previous retirement in March 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> It is thought that this is also to cover for downtime of Virgin's Boeing 787 fleet, but will also allow leverage for the leased A330-200 sub-fleet to provide growth opportunities, opeing up lower-demand routes. The 2 returned A340-600 aircraft, "G-VNAP" and "G-VWIN" were previously leased, but are now owned out-right by Virgin Atlantic.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_Fleet">Current Fleet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Current Fleet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Virgin Atlantic's fleet is operated by Virgin Atlantic Airways Ltd and Virgin Atlantic International Limited.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Operated_by_Virgin_Atlantic_Airways_Limited">Operated by Virgin Atlantic Airways Limited</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Operated by Virgin Atlantic Airways Limited">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Livery">Livery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Livery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:G-VFAB_Boeing_747-400_Virgin_Atlantic_(14622727959).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/G-VFAB_Boeing_747-400_Virgin_Atlantic_%2814622727959%29.jpg/220px-G-VFAB_Boeing_747-400_Virgin_Atlantic_%2814622727959%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/G-VFAB_Boeing_747-400_Virgin_Atlantic_%2814622727959%29.jpg/330px-G-VFAB_Boeing_747-400_Virgin_Atlantic_%2814622727959%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/G-VFAB_Boeing_747-400_Virgin_Atlantic_%2814622727959%29.jpg/440px-G-VFAB_Boeing_747-400_Virgin_Atlantic_%2814622727959%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:G-VFAB_Boeing_747-400_Virgin_Atlantic_(14622727959).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">Boeing 747-400</a> <i>Lady Penelope</i> in <i>Birthday Girl</i> livery in 2014, on approach to <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">New York-JFK</a>, NY, United States</div></div></div>
<p>Virgin's first aircraft were painted with a <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_livery#Eurowhite" title="Aircraft livery">"Eurowhite"</a> design with a red stripe through the centre of the main deck windows. The engines were metallic silver and the tail red with the Virgin logo in white. In the 1990s, the refreshed design was introduced, removing the centre red stripe through the windows, engines were painted red, the Virgin Atlantic titles in grey were added along the main fuselage, and the 'Flying Lady' was introduced to the nose area.
</p><p>In October 2006, with the delivery of G-VRED, Virgin introduced a new design, with the fuselage painted in metallic silver and a revised tail fin, with red and purple features and the Virgin logo. Near the nose of each aircraft is a <a href="/wiki/Pin-up_girl" class="mw-redirect" title="Pin-up girl">pin-up girl</a>, the "Scarlet Lady", carrying a Union flag, which was designed by British artist Ken White, who modelled the motif on the World War II pin-ups of <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Vargas" title="Alberto Vargas">Alberto Vargas</a> – hence the naming one of the fleet <i>Varga Girl</i> (in this case, an A340-600 registered G-VGAS).<sup id="cite_ref-Virgin_Atlantic_press_information_48-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Virgin_Atlantic_press_information-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Each aircraft has a name, usually feminine, such as <i>Ladybird</i>, <i>Island Lady</i>, and <i>Ruby Tuesday</i>, but some are linked to registrations (e.g. G-VFIZ became <i>Bubbles</i>). A couple are commemorative names (e.g. G-VEIL—<i>Queen of the Skies</i>—which was named by <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> on 7 April 2004, marking the centenary of the <a href="/wiki/Entente_Cordiale" title="Entente Cordiale">Entente Cordiale</a>; this frame exited the fleet in April 2016). An exception is <i>Spirit of Sir Freddie</i>. An early Boeing 747, it was named in honour of <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Laker" title="Freddie Laker">Freddie Laker</a> of Laker Airways, who helped Virgin Atlantic following the demise of his own airline. G-VFAB—<i>Lady Penelope</i>—gained a special livery to celebrate Virgin Atlantic's 21st birthday. G-VFAB, <i>Lady Penelope</i>, exited the fleet in September 2016 after 21 years of service and was subsequently parted out.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The current livery dates from 2010 and returns to the "Eurowhite" design featuring purple billboard titles on the fuselage, slight changes to the Scarlet Lady, and new red metallic paint for the aircraft's tail and engines. On aircraft that have winglets, the wingtips are red, with the Virgin logo on the inside facing passengers on board. The Virgin Atlantic logo was also added in purple billboard titles to the underside of the aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents_and_accidents">Incidents and accidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Incidents and accidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>On 5 November 1997, after numerous attempts to shake free the jammed main landing gear of an <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A340-300" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A340-300">Airbus A340-300</a> (G-VSKY) failed, the aircraft en route from Los Angeles to Heathrow, made an emergency landing at Heathrow Airport. The aircraft sustained major damage to the undersides of engines one, two and four, which made contact with the runway surface during landing. The runway surface was also damaged and several runway lights were broken as the right main landing gear wheels broke up during the deceleration. The aircraft was evacuated safely. Two crew members and five passengers sustained minor injuries during the evacuation.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> The damaged aircraft was repaired after the incident and was retired from the Virgin Atlantic fleet in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On 8 February 2005, on board an <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A340-600" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A340-600">Airbus A340-600</a> aircraft (G-VATL) en route from Hong Kong to Heathrow, the fuel control computer system caused a loss of automatic fuel transfer between tanks. The left outboard engine lost power, and shortly afterwards the right outboard engine also began to falter until the crew began to crossfeed fuel manually. The crew diverted to Amsterdam and landed safely. The interim accident report made four safety recommendations addressed to the primary certification bodies for large transport category aircraft (<a href="/wiki/European_Aviation_Safety_Agency" title="European Aviation Safety Agency">EASA</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">FAA</a>), advising on the need for a low-fuel warning system for large aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">
